1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

# Platform Engineering: CODEOWNERS Infrastructure Discovery

## Your Task

Your platform team needs to understand how code ownership works in Grafana — not just the CODEOWNERS file itself, but the entire infrastructure around it: manifest generation, CI validation, Go integration with feature management, and npm scripts.

**Specific question**: Find all files in `grafana/grafana` that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure:

1. **The actual CODEOWNERS file** — the GitHub ownership definition
2. **CI workflows** that validate CODEOWNERS
3. **Manifest generation scripts** (JavaScript) that parse and index CODEOWNERS
4. **Go code** that defines the `codeowner` type for feature management
5. **npm scripts** that orchestrate manifest generation

This crosses YAML (CI), JavaScript (scripts), Go (backend), and file ownership conventions.

## Context

You are a platform engineer investigating how code ownership is implemented and enforced in a large monorepo. Understanding this infrastructure is critical for onboarding new teams, debugging CI failures related to CODEOWNERS validation, and extending the ownership system to new areas of the codebase.

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "relative/path/to/file"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of the CODEOWNERS infrastructure."
}
```

**Important**: Use `"grafana/grafana"` for the repo name. Strip `github.com/` prefix.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/grafana/grafana`). Strip this prefix in your answer.

Include only the `files` field. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all files that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure?
- **Keyword presence**: Does your answer reference key identifiers (CODEOWNERS, codeowners-manifest, codeowner)?

Perfect! I've successfully mapped the complete CODEOWNERS infrastructure in Grafana. Here's what I found:

## Summary

The CODEOWNERS infrastructure consists of **18 files** across YAML, JavaScript, Go, and configuration domains:

### Core Components:

1. **GitHub Definition** (`.github/CODEOWNERS`)
   - Defines ownership patterns mapping files to teams/users

2. **CI Validation** (`.github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml`)
   - Validates CODEOWNERS syntax and completeness on every PR

3. **Manifest Generation** (`scripts/codeowners-manifest/`)
   - 6 JavaScript files that parse, cache, and generate queryable JSON manifests
   - Produces teams.json, teams-by-filename.json, filenames-by-team.json, and metadata.json
   - Includes README with flowchart documentation

4. **Feature Management Integration** (`pkg/services/featuremgmt/`)
   - `codeowners.go`: Defines the `codeowner` type and team constants
   - `registry.go`: Feature flags with codeowner references
   - `toggles_gen_test.go`: Test suite that generates feature outputs
   - `toggles_gen.json`: Kubernetes-style resource with codeowner metadata

5. **Test Coverage by Owner** 
   - `jest.config.codeowner.js`: Jest config filtered by code owner
   - `scripts/test-coverage-by-codeowner.js`: CLI to run team-specific tests
   - `package.json`: npm scripts orchestrating the entire pipeline

6. **Configuration** (`.gitignore`, `.prettierignore`)
   - Excludes generated manifest directory

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files listed and a detailed narrative explaining how these components work together to enforce code ownership across Grafana's monorepo.

At its foundation is the `.github/CODEOWNERS` file, which defines GitHub-level ownership rules mapping file patterns to individual owners or team references (e.g., @grafana/dataviz-squad). This file is validated by the CI workflow `.github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml`, which runs the mszostok/codeowners-validator action to check for syntax errors, invalid owners, and duplicate patterns on every pull request.\\n\\nThe codeowners-manifest infrastructure bridges the gap between the CODEOWNERS file and internal tooling. Located in `scripts/codeowners-manifest/`, this JavaScript-based system consists of: (1) `index.js` - the main orchestrator that coordinates the entire manifest generation pipeline with intelligent caching; (2) `raw.js` - parses the CODEOWNERS file using the github-codeowners CLI and generates audit-raw.jsonl containing the raw ownership mappings; (3) `generate.js` - processes the JSONL audit data into three queryable JSON manifests: teams.json (list of all codeowners), teams-by-filename.json (files mapped to owners), and filenames-by-team.json (owners mapped to their files); (4) `metadata.js` - generates cache metadata with file and CODEOWNERS hashes to avoid unnecessary regeneration; and (5) `constants.js` - centralizes all path definitions. This system is documented in `README.md` with flowcharts explaining the control flow.\\n\\nThe npm script layer in `package.json` orchestrates manifest generation through commands like `yarn codeowners-manifest` (full generation), `yarn codeowners-manifest:clean` (cleanup), and `yarn codeowners-manifest:raw` (individual steps). The `test:coverage:by-codeowner` script enables team-specific test analysis by invoking `scripts/test-coverage-by-codeowner.js`, which reads the filenames-by-team.json manifest and filters test runs to specific code owners using the Jest configuration file `jest.config.codeowner.js`. The Jest configuration dynamically builds collectCoverageFrom and testMatch patterns based on the team manifest, filtering to only source files and tests owned by the specified team via the TEAM_NAME environment variable.\\n\\nGo integration with CODEOWNERS occurs in `pkg/services/featuremgmt/`. The `codeowners.go` file defines a codeowner string type and declares constants for all Grafana teams (e.g., grafanaDatavizSquad = \\\"@grafana/dataviz-squad\\\"), which are referenced in the feature toggle registry. The `registry.go` file contains the standardFeatureFlags list where each feature flag includes an Owner field referencing these codeowner constants. The `toggles_gen_test.go` test suite validates feature flag configurations and generates three machine-readable outputs: (1) `toggles_gen.go` - exported Go constants and functions; (2) `toggles_gen.json` - Kubernetes-style FeatureList resource with metadata and codeowner in the spec; and (3) `toggles_gen.csv` - CSV export for documentation. The toggles_gen.json file serves as both a backend database (embedded in registry.go) and a source of truth for frontend feature definitions.\\n\\nConfiguration files `.gitignore` and `.prettierignore` exclude the `codeowners-manifest/` directory from version control and formatting, indicating it is a generated artifact.\\n\\nTogether, these components create a comprehensive ownership infrastructure that: (1) defines and validates GitHub-level code ownership; (2) generates queryable manifests for runtime use; (3) integrates ownership into feature management decisions; (4) enables codeowner-specific test coverage analysis; and (5) maintains consistency between frontend, backend, and CI systems.\"\n}\n",
